Key Properties\n\n- **Lemma 1:** \\( F(x) \\) is periodic with period \\( \\tfrac{1}{2} \\) (since \\( |\\sin(2\\pi x)| \\) has period \\( \\tfrac{1}{2} \\)), and \\( F(x) \\in [0, 1] \\) for \\( x \\in [0, 1] \\). Maxima occur where \\( |\\sin(2\\pi x)| = 0, \\tfrac{1}{2}, 1 \\) (e.g., \\( x = 0, \\tfrac{1}{12}, \\tfrac{1}{4}, \\tfrac{5}{12}, \\tfrac{1}{2}, etc. \\)), where \\( F(x) = 1 \\).\n\n- **Lemma 2:** \\( G(y) \\) is periodic with period \\( \\tfrac{1}{3} \\) in \\( y \\) (since \\( |\\cos(3\\pi y)| \\) has period \\( \\tfrac{1}{3} \\)), and \\( G(y) \\in [0, 1] \\) for \\( y \\in [0, 1] \\). Minima occur where \\( G(y) = 0 \\) (when \\( |\\cos(3\\pi y)| = \\tfrac{1}{4} \\) or \\( \\tfrac{3}{4} \\)); there are 12 such points in \\([0, 1]\\). Maxima occur where \\( G(y) = 1 \\) (when \\( |\\cos(3\\pi y)| = 0, \\tfrac{1}{2}, 1 \\)); there are 11 such points in \\([0, 1]\\).\n\n- **Lemma 3:** \\( G(F(x)) \\) has period \\( \\tfrac{1}{2} \\) (inherited from \\( F(x) \\)).\n\n- **Lemma 4:** \\( H(0) = G(F(0)) - 0 = G(1) - 0 = 1 \\), and \\( H(1) = G(F(1)) - 1 = G(1) - 1 = 0 \\).\n\n---\n\n#### Step 3. Critical Points and Intervals\n\nThe critical points of \\( F(x) \\) on \\([0, 1]\\) occur where \\( |\\sin(2\\pi x)| = 0, \\tfrac{1}{4}, \\tfrac{1}{2}, \\tfrac{3}{4}, 1 \\). These include:\n- \\( x = 0 \\)\n- \\( x \\approx 0.0402 \\) (from \\( \\arcsin(1/4)/(2\\pi) \\))\n- \\( x = 1/12 \\approx 0.0833 \\)\n- \\( x \\approx 0.1350 \\) (from \\( \\arcsin(3/4)/(2\\pi) \\))\n- \\( x = 1/4 = 0.25 \\)\n- \\( x \\approx 0.3650 \\) (from \\( (\\pi - \\arcsin(3/4))/(2\\pi) \\))\n- \\( x = 5/12 \\approx 0.4167 \\)\n- \\( x \\approx 0.4598 \\) (from \\( (\\pi - \\arcsin(1/4))/(2\\pi) \\))\n- \\( x = 1/2 = 0.5 \\)\n- And symmetric points in \\([0.5, 1]\\): \\( x \\approx 0.5402, 0.5833, 0.6350, 0.75, 0.8650, 0.9167, 0.9598, 1 \\)\n\nThese 17 points divide \\([0, 1]\\) into 16 subintervals. In \\([0, 1/2]\\), there are 8 subintervals; in \\([1/2, 1]\\), there are 8 subintervals.\n\n---\n\n#### Step 4. Evaluate \\( H(x) \\) at Critical Points\n\nAt critical points where \\( F(x) = 0 \\) or \\( F(x) = 1 \\), \\( G(F(x)) = 1 \\), so \\( H(x) = 1 - x > 0 \\) for \\( x < 1 \\). At \\( x = 1 \\), \\( H(1) = 0 \\).\n\n---\n\n#### Step 5. Zero Count of \\( H(x) \\) Using Intermediate Value Theorem\n\nOn each subinterval, \\( F(x) \\) is continuous and strictly monotonic (increasing or decreasing) and maps onto \\([0, 1]\\). Thus, for each of the 12 zeros of \\( G(y) \\) in \\([0, 1]\\), there is exactly one \\( x \\) in the subinterval where \\( F(x) = y \\), so \\( G(F(x)) = 0 \\) and \\( H(x) = -x < 0 \\). Similarly, for each of the 11 points where \\( G(y) = 1 \\), there is exactly one \\( x \\) where \\( G(F(x)) = 1 \\) and \\( H(x) = 1 - x > 0 \\).\n\nThe points where \\( G(F(x)) = 0 \\) and \\( G(F(x)) = 1 \\) are interleaved in \\( x \\)-order on each subinterval (since the corresponding \\( y \\)-values are interleaved and \\( F \\) is monotonic). Thus, on each subinterval:\n- At endpoints, \\( H(x) > 0 \\).\n- At points where \\( G(F(x)) = 0 \\), \\( H(x) < 0 \\).\n- Between each pair of consecutive points where \\( G(F(x)) = 0 \\), there is a point where \\( G(F(x)) = 1 \\) and \\( H(x) > 0 \\).\n\nBy continuity:\n- Between the left endpoint and the first \\( G(F(x)) = 0 \\) point, \\( H \\) changes from positive to negative, so one zero.\n- Between the last \\( G(F(x)) = 0 \\) point and the right endpoint, \\( H \\) changes from negative to positive, so one zero.\n- Between each pair of consecutive \\( G(F(x)) = 0 \\) points, \\( H \\) changes from negative to positive to negative, so two zeros.\n\nWith 12 points where \\( G(F(x)) = 0 \\), there are 11 intervals between them, each contributing 2 zeros, plus 2 zeros from the endpoints, so total zeros per subinterval = \\( 2 + 2 \\times 11 = 24 \\).\n\nIn \\([0, 1]\\), there are 16 subintervals, so zeros in \\((0, 1)\\) are \\( 16 \\times 24 = 384 \\). Including \\( H(1) = 0 \\), total zeros are \\( 384 + 1 = 385 \\).\n\n---\n\n#### Step 6. Final Answer\n\nEach zero of \\( H(x) \\) corresponds to a unique intersection point of the graphs. Therefore, the number of intersections is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{385}\n\\]"
